{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-11-18 01:13:35","updatedTime":"2020-11-18 01:13:35","title":"Wahoo RIVAL Multisport GPS Watch In-Depth Review","link":"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/?p=120050","description":"<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-In-Depth-Review.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-In-Depth-Review\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-In-Depth-Review_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-In-Depth-Review\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>It’s here. Finally. After years of rumors, leaks, and even a high crimes story I’ve got for another day, Wahoo’s first watch has landed – the aptly named Wahoo RIVAL, a $379 entrant in a field full of competitive options.</p> \n<p>And to begin, despite what clickbait headlines you might read today – no, it’s not a Garmin killer. Nor is it a Suunto killer, nor a Polar killer, nor a COROS killer. It’s not even a killer of the already dead TomTom multisport watches.</p> \n<p>But that doesn’t mean it’s not promising. <strong>It is</strong>. And one day, it might take some sales from those companies above – undoubtedly. And while Wahoo has&nbsp; along road ahead of them, the company also has a long history of coming into the market and causing grief for incumbents. Remember CompuTrainer? Yup – <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2017/02/computrainer-ceases-production.html\">Wahoo was the legit ‘CompuTrainer Killer’</a>. Of course, wearables are a far more established, widespread, and a more difficult market to master – as the RIVAL shows.</p> \n<p>For Wahoo’s first go at this, they’re squarely targeting the triathlon market. Specifically – swim, bike, run. RIVAL’s marquee feature is a new touchless transition mode that automatically changes the sport modes on your watch as you iterate through your triathlon race. It even allows you to ‘undo’ mid-race if you or the algorithm makes a mistake, and to top that off, lets you get super precise on transition splits after the fact in the app <em>before</em> it uploads to 3rd party sites like Strava or TrainingPeaks. It’s super cool.</p> \n<p>But, we’ll get into all the features at a high level in the next section, before diving into them in even more detail later on in the sports section. I legit went out and did a mock-triathlon in mid-November in Northern Europe to test it all out. You’re welcome.</p> \n<p>Finally, note that Wahoo sent me a media loaner RIVAL for the purposes of testing. As usual, afterwards I’ll send it back to them and go out and pick up my own through normal retail channels. I don’t take any money, ads, or products from companies I review. If you’ve found this review useful, feel free to hit up the links at the end of the site. Or, consider <a href=\"http://www.dcrainmaker.com/support\">becoming a DCR Supporter</a>.</p> \n<p>With that – let’s get on with it.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Quick Summary:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1362.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1362\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1362_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1362\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>As I started off with, RIVAL is a triathlon watch, which means it can cover swim/bike/run both indoors and outdoors. So you can do openwater swims, pool swims, use a power meter on the bike – and it’ll even pair with and record running power data from a Stryd running power meter. It’s got a barometric altimeter for more accurate elevation data. It’s got the optical HR sensor in the back for workout HR data (including while swimming). For the most part, the features on the RIVAL are pretty basic. They’re roughly on-par with a <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2013/07/tomtom-runner-multisport.html\">TomTom Multisport GPS watch from 7 years ago</a>, just with a few features in different buckets. It’s just that the RIVAL looks a heck of a lot better, and also has more robust sensor support (inversely, TomTom had better activity tracking data, GPS/HR accuracy, and full structured workout support).</p> \n<p>– GPS watch with claimed battery life of 24 hours GPS, and 14 days standby<br /> – Color 240x240px screen (64 colors) with Gorilla Glass<br /> – Barometric altimeter<br /> – Optical HR sensor (for workout and 24×7 tracking)<br /> – Ambient light sensor<br /> – Water-resistant to 5ATM (50 meters)<br /> – Changeable wrist straps<br /> – Broadcasts your heart rate over Bluetooth Smart &amp; ANT+<br /> – Livetrack support when paired with phone<br /> – Multisport/triathlon mode, including touchless transitions<br /> – Has timer &amp; stopwatch<br /> – Supports ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart sensors<br /> – Supports running power meters like Stryd<br /> – Supports Running Dynamics from TICKR-X (new 2020 variant)<br /> – Uploads to 3rd party sites like Strava, TrainingPeaks, Dropbox, and tons more</p> \n<p>Now here’s the thing – I’m sure Wahoo won’t terribly like me listing out all the things that aren’t in this watch, but when there’s no baseline to establish from, and no clarity on Wahoo’s own site, this is the kind of detail people actually want. Else, one can just read marketing fluff (or regurgitated marketing fluff somewhere else):</p> \n<p>– No structured workout support<br /> – No courses/routing/navigation/compass support<br /> – No maps or breadcrumb trails<br /> – No music<br /> – No contactless payments<br /> – No 24×7 HR data in the app<br /> – No sleep tracking, stairs, or most other activity tracking metrics<br /> – No watch time alarms<br /> – No sport alerts (e.g. heart rate zones, speed, power, cadence, etc…)<br /> – No 3rd party apps on the watch itself<br /> – No Strava Live Segments on device itself<br /> – No training load, recover, or other physiological type metrics<br /> – No anything else I didn’t explicitly list above.</p> \n<p>Now, as for whether or not these features get rolled out – undoubtedly some will. When is a tougher question. Wahoo says they want to aim for roughly a quarterly release cadence for major releases, but may drop smaller things earlier/when ready. Jose Mendez, Director of Product Development for Wahoo Fitness noted that “We’re launching a business, a product category, we’re not launching a product”, and that ultimately, “This is our dipping our toe in the water.”</p> \n<p>And I’m glad to see them loosely committing to a quarterly release cycle, but the simple reality here is that they need to be more explicit in what they’re planning on doing. That’s what both Suunto and <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2019/05/vantage-v-titan-suunto-roadmap-xert-ios.html\">Polar did</a> <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2019/10/polar-releases-major-new-features-to-vantage-m-v-series.html\">when they</a> <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2018/09/the-new-polar-vantage-series-everything-you-ever-wanted-to-know.html#whats-new\">arrived on the</a> scene with heavily under-featured watches. And while Wahoo might believe they’d be giving their competitors an advantage – that’s a pretty hard line to swallow.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">What’s in the box:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-Front-Box.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-Front-Box\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-Front-Box_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-Front-Box\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I really like the RIVAL box. It’s easily one of my favorite watch boxes out there. And sure, it’s very similar to Wahoo’s ROAM box, but still…it’s super nice.</p> \n<p>It unfolds out to the left, telling you to never lose focus. Ironically, a number of my video shots lost focus on this. But that’s neither here nor there.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-BOX-Open.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-BOX-Open\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-BOX-Open_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-BOX-Open\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a><br /> Once you do manage to focus, it’s super clear this is all about triathlon. You can see what’s clearly a mass triathlon start up top, followed by a triathlete on a triathlon bike, followed by someone realizing they should have stopped after the bike.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Waoo-Rival-Focused-On.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Waoo-Rival-Focused-On\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Waoo-Rival-Focused-On_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Waoo-Rival-Focused-On\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Sliding the box out from itself, you’ve got the watch:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-Rival-Slip-OpenBox.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Wahoo-Rival-Slip-OpenBox\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-Rival-Slip-OpenBox_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Wahoo-Rival-Slip-OpenBox\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Take all that stuff out, and here’s what you’ve got:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-Rival-Box-Parts.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Wahoo-Rival-Box-Parts\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-Rival-Box-Parts_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Wahoo-Rival-Box-Parts\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Here’s a better picture of that. Basically, it’s just two little manual booklets, the watch, and the charging puck:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-Parts.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-Parts\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/Wahoo-RIVAL-Parts_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"Wahoo-RIVAL-Parts\" width=\"723\" height=\"478\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>The charging puck is…well…round. those, more in line with a Fenix 6 series watch. Here’s the rolling pin, first with a bulkier set of watches:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1446.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1450\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1450_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1450\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Ok, with that let’s start using it.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">The Basics:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1369.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1369\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1369_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1369\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>In this section I typically cover some of the basic user interface aspects, such as how to navigate the menus, charging, app connectivity basics, as well as daily activity tracking type features (steps/etc). For the sport-specific features you’ll want to hit up the next section.</p> \n<p>To begin, the RIVAL has five dedicated buttons. The screen is (thankfully) not a touchscreen device. It’s not that I’m opposed to touchscreens, it’s just that for hyper-sport specific purposes, I rarely find them useful. Even in the case of the Suunto 9 or Polar Vantage V series that have touchscreens, I very rarely use the touchscreen elements. The buttons work better. Of course, there are good touch-screen implementations, but they tend to skew non-sport focused (like the Apple Watch). The middle-ground options like the Garmin Venu series touchscreens are kinda ‘meh’ for usability purposes.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1370.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1370\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1370_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1370\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Speaking of ‘meh’, so is the RIVAL’s user interface. The good thing is I expect it’ll <span style=\"text-decoration: line-through;\">change</span> mature. As I sit here and try and explain how this works, I realize that’s a surprisingly complicated concept. Mostly because it’s not super intuitive. I guess to begin, the upper right button is how you access your smartphone notifications. These are read-only, so there’s no responding to notifications here.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1379.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1379\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1379_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1379\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>The watch can be configured to automatically enter do-not-disturb mode at a given time each day, or, you can always manually set DND by just long-holding the upper right button.</p> \n<p>Next, the middle-right button lets you select from a predefined list of sports to start. These are: Running (GPS), Treadmill, Lap Swimming, Openwater Swim, Cycling (GPS), KICKR, Strength, Yoga, Triathlon. However, you can also make your own profiles (more on that later).</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1383.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1383\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1383_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1383\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>While the indoor cycling option is explicitly labeled ‘KICKR’, the reality is that you can use it for any indoor training, and it’ll pair with any ANT+ FE-C trainer. But we’ll talk about all the sports bits down below.</p> \n<p>Next, the bottom right button – this…this is where things get confusing. This is essentially the same as the middle right button, but it bypasses the sport selection, and jumps straight to the last sport you used. However, if you press the lower right button a second time, it’ll show the data fields for that sport, then a third time it’ll show your heart rate for the last 2 hours, and press it one last time and it (might) show you elevation (if on an outdoor activity):</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1384.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1384\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1384_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1384\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>The bottom left button iterates through the exact same way as the bottom right button, but in reverse. What Wahoo is attempting to do here is basically bridge the divide between the ‘sport’ side of the house (as in, when you choose a given sport to start a workout), and the normal ‘widget’ side of the house, which is where you’d expect to see things like daily steps, 24×7 HR data, etc… Except, in this implementation they’re all confusingly mixed together, and atop that, if you press the lower left/right buttons (purposefully or caught on your jacket), then it immediately begins GPS search.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1389.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1389\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1389_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1389\" width=\"235\" height=\"157\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1385.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1385\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1385_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1385\" width=\"235\" height=\"157\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1386.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1386\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1386_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1386\" width=\"235\" height=\"157\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Wahoo says the reason they did this is because people would get confused on a Garmin watch trying to get to something like the compass or weather widgets mid-workout, and thus couldn’t easily remember/figure out how to get back to those. And yes, I actually agree with that. It can be tough for non-savvy users to figure out.</p> \n<p>But in this context, the opposite is more annoying. I don’t want to be in workout mode anytime I’m trying to check a widget for the other 23 hours of the day I’m not working out. Not to mention, the RIVAL doesn’t yet have compass mode or weather widgets or anything else. I think ideally their concept would only work if you were in a workout mode, allowing you to see those non-workout widgets. But unless in workout mode, don’t show me workout data pages for a sport I’m most definitely not doing this moment. In any event, I think Wahoo is listening to the feedback around this, so hopefully we’ll see some tweaks.</p> \n<p>Next, you can long-hold the bottom left button to get to settings. This includes things like pairing sensors, a simple stopwatch &amp; timer, workout history, and turning off the watch.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1391.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1391\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1391_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1391\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1390.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1390\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1390_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1390\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>There are no wake-up alarms at this point, though admittedly I can’t remember the last time I set the alarm on my watch as opposed to just using my phone.</p> \n<p>Next, you can access the different widgets by double-holding the lower two buttons together, which changes the watch-face data fields. Honestly, this is a bit confusing too.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1392.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1392\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1392_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1392\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1393.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1393\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1393_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1393\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>However, you can customize the watch face, from four different options:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.14.48.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-17 10.14.48\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.14.48_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-17 10.14.48\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.14.54.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-17 10.14.54\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.14.54_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-17 10.14.54\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>You can see above you can also tweak the seconds, date, and accent color.</p> \n<p>When it comes to the backlight, you can manually enable it by pressing the upper left button. There’s no raise to wake or gesture support, though, the backlight should automatically stay-on the entire time during a workout at night.</p> \n<p>I’d describe the backlight as ‘fine’ for my pretty good eyes. Not glow fantastic, but…well…fine. I’ve used it on many night workouts without issues seeing it. In a semi-related setting, you can change between light mode and dark mode, between off/auto/on.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.15.08.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-17 10.15.08\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.15.08_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"2020-11-17 10.15.08\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Finally, when it comes to things like tracking steps, heart rate, stairs, sleep, etc… it’s incredibly minimal right now. The watch itself will show your current step total for the day against your static step goal (which you can customize). You can see that on the watch face, as well as your current heart rate:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1392-1.jpg\"><img style=\"margin: 0px; border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1392\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1392_thumb-1.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1392\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1393-1.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1393\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1393_thumb-1.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1393\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>And as shown earlier, you can also see the last two hours of heart rate data in the widget roll.</p> \n<p>But when it comes to the app…there’s almost nothing. The Wahoo app will only show you the total steps you did each day that week, and only for the current week you’re in. Once the clock strikes midnight you can’t see/access that data anymore within the Wahoo app. Here’s the before/after midnight look at things for steps. There’s no method to look at last week’s steps, or to dive in and see details about today’s steps (such as how they allocate over the course of the day). That little settings icon there simply toggles other week summary pages like ones for cycling, gym workouts, and swimming:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.18.05.png\"><img style=\"display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 00.18.05\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.18.05_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 00.18.05\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.19.16.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 00.19.16\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.19.16_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 00.19.16\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>And that’s it. There’s no sleep tracking, nor is there any way to look at heart rate data. Wahoo says they are storing that HR data, as well as step data. And that better reporting is definitely in the pipeline.</p> \n<p>For now, that data is also sent over to Apple Health and Google Fit.&nbsp; For example, you can see tidbits of this in Apple Health, but it’s sporadic at best. I’m missing entire days for both steps and heart rate, and even some days it only plots a single data point. Just one second’s worth. Wahoo says they’re aware of this issue and hope to have it resolved shortly after launch.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.24.23.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 00.24.23\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.24.23_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 00.24.23\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.22.45.png\"><img style=\"display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 00.22.45\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.22.45_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 00.22.45\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.23.12.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 00.23.12\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-00.23.12_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 00.23.12\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I get it, this is likely low-priority stuff. While I think it’s important to feed data into Apple Health and Google Fit, I wonder how many normal people actually ever use that data put there (in a cross-pollination kinda way).</p> \n<p>In my mind what’s far more important is getting clear reporting of 24×7 type metrics within the Wahoo app, beyond just this week’s step totals.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Sport Details:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1403.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1403\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1403_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1403\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>If you’re buying the RIVAL, you’re doing so for the purposes of sport – and likely more specifically, as a triathlete (at least for now). So throughout the course of this section I’ll dive into all the sport features, including doing a test triathlon.</p> \n<p>To start with recording a workout (or race), you’ll press the middle right button, which brings open the sport menu:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1406.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1406\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1406_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1406\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>It’s here you’ll choose the sport mode you want. By default that’s: Running (GPS), Treadmill, Lap Swimming, Openwater Swim, Cycling (GPS), KICKR, Strength, Yoga, Triathlon.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1407.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1407\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1407_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1407\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>However, from within the app you can make your own sport profiles by selecting ‘Add Workout profile”. From there you’ve got three options: Using a template, duplicating one of your previous profiles, and creating a new profile from the ground up. If you choose a template there are piles of sport modes per overall category (5 types of ‘running’, 10 types of cycling, etc…):</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.07.02.png\"><img style=\"display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.07.02\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.07.02_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.07.02\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.07.51.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.07.51\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.07.51_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.07.51\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.07.57.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.07.57\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.07.57_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.07.57\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>While some of these do include more sport-specific data files, a number of them are basically just a different icon. For example, choosing the skiing one just gives you the empty shell without any data pages specific to skiing (or at all for that matter). I think this is an area where they’ve just outlined a starting point, but would ultimately offer actual differences in the profiles down the road. For example on a Polar watch, there are substantial fine-tuned differences in calorie profiles. On a Garmin watch if you select skiing you get specific skiing metrics, or specific paddling metrics for certain water sports.</p> \n<p>Using the duplicate a profile or build a profile from the ground up isn’t honestly much different. For any given profile you’ve basically got four key things you can tweak + the data pages. So you can enable/disable optical HR, GPS, Auto-Pause, and Auto-Lap. I guess five things if you include the name of the profile.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.49.25.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.49.25\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.49.25_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.49.25\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.49.16.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.49.16\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.49.16_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.49.16\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>From a data page standpoint, you can create multiple custom data pages with up to six data fields per page. These are then ranked in order of preference, so you can use the PerfectView zoom function if you want to, on the fly.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.49.38.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.49.38\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.49.38_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.49.38\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.52.26.png\"><img style=\"display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.52.26\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.52.26_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.52.26\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.53.10.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 16.53.10\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-16.53.10_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 16.53.10\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Wahoo has long gotten props for their customization of data fields via the app – and it’s true, it’s definitely good. On the flipside, you can’t customize data fields or sport modes mid-workout on the device itself. One of these days companies from both sides of that divide will allow us to do both, depending on our preferences.</p> \n<p>Looking at the data fields, here’s a quick gallery of what that looks like with a few different data pages. Note that there is an elevation and heart rate graph page in the mix.</p> \n<a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/dsc_1409\"><img width=\"200\" height=\"132\" srcset=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1415-200x132.jpg 200w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1415-124x82.jpg 124w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1413-720x480@2x.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" /></a> \n<a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/dsc_1411\"><img width=\"200\" srcset=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-200x132.jpg 200w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-124x82.jpg 124w,
