https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-300x200.jpg 300w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-278x185.jpg 278w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-125x83.jpg 125w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-768x512@2x.jpg 1536w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1411-720x480@2x.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" /></a> \n<a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/dsc_1410\"><img width=\"200\" height=\"132\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-200x132.jpg\" class=\"attachment-archive_crop size-archive_crop\" alt=\"\" srcset=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-200x132.jpg 200w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-124x82.jpg 124w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-768x512.jpg 768w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-720x480.jpg 720w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-300x200.jpg 300w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-278x185.jpg 278w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-125x83.jpg 125w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-768x512@2x.jpg 1536w, https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1410-720x480@2x.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 200px) 100vw, 200px\" /></a> \n<p>Above you’ll see some data pages that are 1 field in size, and others that are 6 fields in size. Technically speaking, that’s actually the same data page. Wahoo has something they call ‘PerfectView’, which basically means you can squeeze the bottom two buttons together mid-workout to add or remove fields based on a predefined priority order – the order we set in the app settings above.</p> \n<p>This is the exact same concept as on their bike computers, except it just requires the two button press here instead of up/down in the menus. This feature can be handy out on a long-run where you just want to get rid of everything but time, or heart rate – whatever you value the most.</p> \n<p>Ok, with everything all set, let’s go back to running mode and head out for a run. As you get GPS signal it’ll loop around the outside of the watch showing the GPS satellite reception until it’s locked. Generally this was about the same time duration as the Garmin FR745 and Polar Grit X units I was using most days concurrently. That’s logical, because it’s likely the exact same GPS chipset. Wahoo uses Sony for their RIVAL, just as Polar and Garmin do for all their recent units.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1408.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1408\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1408_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1408\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Once locked, it’ll change that play/start button to green, and you’re good to go. At this point, it’s honestly just like any other GPS watch – you run/bike/whatever, and it shows your data metrics in real-time.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h21m29s106.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h21m29s106\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h21m29s106_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h21m29s106\" width=\"720\" height=\"405\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>You’ve got auto-lap if you configured it, using either distance or time. As well as auto-pause if you’ve got that enabled too.</p> \n<p>Also, while the RIVAL is supposed to support the ANT+ Running Dynamics standard, it appears there’s still some bugs there. In my testing, using a non-Wahoo strap that’s capable of Running Dynamics isn’t enumerating any data at this point. Only the <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2020/05/wahoos-new-2020-tickr-tickr-x-in-depth-review.html\">TICKR X (2020 edition)</a> is working. In my case, I created a running dynamics workout page for the run profile, and then paired up the TICKR X. Here’s a very brief test showing the vertical oscillation and ground contact time data from the TICKR X:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.22.55.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-17 10.22.55\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.22.55_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-17 10.22.55\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.23.23.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-17 10.23.23\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-17-10.23.23_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-17 10.23.23\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I also tried the <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2020/09/garmin-hrm-pro-chest-strap-depth-review.html\">Garmin HRM-PRO</a> (which follows the ANT+ standard for Running Dynamics), but that didn’t enumerate any data. In theory, the RIVAL should eventually work with the HRM-PRO, HRM-TRI, and HRM-RUN straps from Garmin, which properly transmit that data like the TICKR X 2020 does (after all, you can use a TICKR X 2020 strap with a Garmin device and get running dynamics data).</p> \n<p>Note that you’ll likely still see a slight difference there, as Wahoo doesn’t actually leverage the exact same fields as Garmin. For example Wahoo doesn’t do GCT Balance, whereas Garmin does. It’s unclear if those added metrics will make the cut once compatibility is sorted out.</p> \n<p>Next, for running specifically, it does support running power. Or more specifically, displaying and recording power while running. if paired with a compatible sensor transmitting power using the ANT+ or BLE power standards. You can use any of the cycling running fields in the running profile, and it’ll record that data. It’s not as extensive as COROS’s running power support (natively or for Stryd). But if you just want to display or record the data no-fuss, this works just fine. However, it won’t display it in the Wahoo app itself. But it will to 3rd parties.</p> \n<p>Here’s a run from this weekend with Stryd power, shown on TrainingPeaks:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-33.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-33.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"321\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>After the run is complete, you’ll see your summary metrics. This is super basic and doesn’t include maps/route outlines, time in zones, or anything else. Just a list of top-line metrics, followed by your lap splits:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1339.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1339\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1339_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1339\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1344.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1344\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1344_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1344\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Switching topics over to indoor training, it’s all basically identical to outdoor training, except without GPS. For example, on a trainer you’ll select the option labeled ‘KICKR’. While the indoor cycling option is explicitly labeled ‘KICKR’, the reality is that you can use it for any indoor training, and it’ll pair with any ANT+ FE-C trainer. Though you can’t execute any structured workouts on it yet.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1424.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1424\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1424_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1424\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Once in a workout if you want to use control mode, you can two-button hold the lower left buttons, and then manually set a new target one digit at a time (meaning, to set 315w, you first set the 3 using up/down, then the 1, then the 5.)&nbsp; Realistically, nobody’s going to do that. So I’ll just wait for actual structured workout support.</p> \n<p>In my case, I used TrainerRoad and Zwift, and then just recorded the workout as well on the RIVAL. Mid-workout you’ll get data details just like with other sports:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-10h37m46s161.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-10h37m46s161\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-10h37m46s161_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-10h37m46s161\" width=\"720\" height=\"413\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>While I had some earlier bugs with trainers, in the most recent firmware update I’ve used it with various trainers recording the data without issue.</p> \n<p>Next, we’ve got triathlon mode. In this mode you’ll iterate from swim to bike to run (with transitions as well). While at present there isn’t the ability to create your own custom multisport mode, Wahoo says it’s coming. Also, you can technically do something like a swim-run by long-holding the upper right button mid-workout, which will select a different sport profile. You can do this indefinitely, so basically, you can create a manual on-the-fly multisport mode.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1428.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1428\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1428_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1428\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1427.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1427\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1427_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1427\" width=\"355\" height=\"237\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>In my case, I went out and swam in very chilly water. I jumped in, swore a bunch, and then swam. I kept swearing however.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h23m35s915.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h23m35s915\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h23m35s915_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h23m35s915\" width=\"720\" height=\"405\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Once I was done with freezing my ass off, I got out of the water and headed to my bike. However, notably, I did *NOT* press any buttons on the RIVAL. I wanted to see how Wahoo’s new ‘Touchless Transitions’ feature worked. This feature is supposed to automatically detect each leg of the race, and transition your watch appropriately to the correct sport. Initially when I got to my bike, it was still showing swim. By this point I had walked down the 50-75m dock, got my cycling shoes on, and put on my coat for the ride.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m30s435.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m30s435\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m30s435_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m30s435\" width=\"720\" height=\"479\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>However, a short time later it updated to show T1, and you can actually see it backdate the T1 and Swim times (above it shows 16:03, and then below it shows 15:51).</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m45s070.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m45s070\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m45s070_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h31m45s070\" width=\"720\" height=\"479\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Of course, you’re now looking at the <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2019/05/wahoo-element-roam-cycling-gps-in-depth-review.html\">Wahoo ROAM</a>. That’s because before I started my ‘race’, I placed the ROAM on my handlebars, and I held the menu button down and entered ‘Multisport mode’, which basically becomes a mirror of the Wahoo RIVAL watch. It’s basically the same concept as <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2019/06/garmins-triathlon-mode-extended-display.html\">Garmin’s not-well-known screen mirroring that I posted about a year ago</a>. Once paired together, the RIVAL transmits data to the ROAM, though the ROAM doesn’t record anything else. It’s just like AirPlay (or casting) from your phone to a TV screen. This works for *ANY* Wahoo ELEMNT/BOLT/ROAM bike computer.</p> \n<p>In any case, with my bike unlocked from the post, I headed out to my transition line, which was the start of the bike path. I had decided ahead of time that’d be my mount/dismount/finish line. Also, I didn’t take my wetsuit off. It was far too cold for that. November and all:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m58s475.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m58s475\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m58s475_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m58s475\" width=\"720\" height=\"405\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>In any case, I left T1, and about 45 seconds later the RIVAL (and along with it ROAM), switched to cycling. In this case, it backdated the start of cycling to about 20 seconds earlier. So not quite perfect, but fine for now. We’ll fix it afterwards. And again, you can ALWAYS manually advance through the sports just like you have on any other watch, in this case by pressing the middle right button.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m10s702.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m10s702\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m10s702_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h35m10s702\" width=\"720\" height=\"479\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I was a bit surprised it took RIVAL this long to detect cycling, since in this case I had a power meter paired, so logically as soon as I started pedaling more than a second or two, I’d have expected it to switch over. But Wahoo says at this point the algorithm doesn’t yet take into account sensor data, rather, just internal assumptions in the watch itself.</p> \n<p>Further, and probably even cooler – you can always ‘undo’ a transition/sport change. So if you accidentally advance to T2 while on the bike, you can simply hold the upper right to undo it back to cycling. Super cool.</p> \n<p>While riding, I kept an eye on the ROAM/RIVAL connection. One of the things I’d seen in the past with Garmin’s triathlon mirroring mode, is that it’s sometimes prone to drop-outs. And that was the case here with Wahoo’s as well. While my triathlon test bike segment was short (just 10KM), it did drop out towards the end for my guessing 15+ seconds. When it did that, data updating stopped.</p> \n<p>That aside, one of the data fields I loved on the ROAM though was the overall triathlon stats, showing my splits for each segment. I don’t know why, but this was just cool.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h37m07s272.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h37m07s272\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h37m07s272_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h37m07s272\" width=\"720\" height=\"479\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I rolled back into transition, and it took about 15 seconds for it to switch to showing T2. Then, as I left my bike behind, I ran out to my transition line. It switched over to ‘Running’ automatically, ironically almost exactly on the transition line. Of course, I suspect detecting running is pretty easy by comparison to cycling. Then I ran. And it did its thing.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h39m43s021.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h39m43s021\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h39m43s021_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-11h39m43s021\" width=\"720\" height=\"481\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I then finished up my run and stopped the watch like any normal human (or normal watch).</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h24m16s657.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h24m16s657\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h24m16s657_thumb.png\" alt=\"vlcsnap-2020-11-17-12h24m16s657\" width=\"720\" height=\"405\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Afterwards, it gave me a summary of all the splits:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-12.33.46.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-11 12.33.46\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-12.33.46_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"2020-11-11 12.33.46\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>However, probably my favorite feature on RIVAL isn’t on RIVAL itself – it’s on the smartphone app, which allows you to edit (dynamically) the exact start/end points of each segment in that triathlon. So if auto-detect didn’t work, or if your brain to hand signals didn’t work, you can easily and quickly fix it afterwards. Silly easy. You just drag the start/end point to where you want it on the map….and done.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-14.26.01.jpg\"><img style=\"display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-11 14.26.01\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-14.26.01_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"2020-11-11 14.26.01\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-14.27.05.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-11 14.27.05\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-14.27.05_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-11 14.27.05\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-14.28.35.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-11 14.28.35\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-11-14.28.35_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-11 14.28.35\" width=\"237\" height=\"510\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>In fact, the key bit here is that Wahoo will actually <em>wait</em> before uploading any multisport workout/race to 3rd party sites like Strava, until you’ve reviewed it. Even cooler is that you can undo and redo this as many times as you’d like on a given workout/race. It’s awesome. So awesome. Albeit, it’s unfortunate that the coolest and probably most marquee set of features on the RIVAL is something that realistically very few people are going to use over the next 6-9 months due to the world situation.</p> \n<p>Last but not least, and perhaps somewhat out of order, is that the Rival can pair to ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart sensors. These include:</p> \n<p>ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart power meters<br /> ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart heart rate straps<br /> ANT+ FE-C trainers<br /> ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart cycling speed sensors<br /> ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart cycling cadence sensors</p> \n<p>You can pair sensors either via the smartphone app, or on the watch itself – just like you would on a Wahoo ELEMNT series unit:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1430.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1430\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1430_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1430\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>And here’s what it looks like via the app, including the ability to rename sensors:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-19.34.01.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 19.34.01\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-19.34.01_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 19.34.01\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a>&nbsp;<a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-19.34.08.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"2020-11-16 19.34.08\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/2020-11-16-19.34.08_thumb.png\" alt=\"2020-11-16 19.34.08\" width=\"357\" height=\"770\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Additionally, for broadcasting of data, the RIVAL will broadcast out your heart rate (as measured by the optical HR sensor) over both ANT+ &amp; Bluetooth Smart. You can toggle this on app or watch, and it’ll broadcast all the time behind the scenes.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1432.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1432\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1432_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1432\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Now before we wrap up this section, note that the RIVAL does support pool swims. Given the current situation, I wasn’t able to get a pool swim in, however, the core metrics including lengths, distance, pace, stroke count, stroke rate, and calories are supported. You can customize the pool size from preset options (e.g. 50m, 25y, etc…), or custom options. It seems to allow a minimum down to 1 yard/meter in length, and a maximum 99m/y in length:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1434.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1434\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1434_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1434\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Notably however, you can also do the same lap-editing as in triathlon mode – but even more extensive with merging of lengths, splitting of lengths, or changing of times. That’s another super cool feature that nobody else really has, though unfortunately again – another super cool feature that won’t likely get as much use given various pool restrictions around the world.</p> \n<p>With that, we’ve covered all there is to cover for now in the sports realm of RIVAL. While Wahoo is saying that functions like structured workout support is coming, there isn’t an exact timeframe for that. Hopefully, since much of the underlying code for cycling would already exist in their ELEMNT bike computer series, the timeframes for implementing this (or more simplistic interval workouts) will make it to the RIVAL sooner rather than later.</p> \n<p>I’ll attempt to circle back in update posts when major features are added. So with that, let’s dive into accuracy.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">GPS Accuracy:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1438.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1438\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1438_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1438\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>There’s likely no topic that stirs as much discussion and passion as GPS accuracy.&nbsp; A watch could fall apart and give you dire electrical shocks while doing so, but if it shows you on the wrong side of the road?&nbsp; Oh hell no, bring on the fury of the internet!</p> \n<p>GPS accuracy can be looked at in a number of different ways, but I prefer to look at it using a number of devices in real-world scenarios across a vast number of activities.&nbsp; I use 2-6 other devices at once, trying to get a clear picture of how a given set of devices handles conditions on a certain day.&nbsp; Conditions include everything from tree/building cover to weather.</p> \n<p>Over the years, I’ve continued to tweak my GPS testing methodology.&nbsp; For example, I don’t place two units next to each other on my wrists, as that can impact signal. If I do so, I’ll put a thin fabric spacer of about 1”/3cm between them (I didn’t do that on any of my Wahoo RIVAL activities however, all workouts only had a single device per wrist).&nbsp; But often I’ll simply carry other units by the straps, or attach them to the shoulder straps of my hydration backpack.&nbsp; Plus, wearing multiple watches on the same wrist is well known to impact optical HR accuracy.</p> \n<p>Next, as noted, I use just my daily training routes.&nbsp; Using a single route over and over again isn’t really indicative of real-world conditions, it’s just indicative of one trail – that’s why I use routes all over the place.&nbsp; The workouts you see here are just my normal daily workouts.</p> \n<p>The Wahoo RIVAL has a Sony GPS chipset, which is the same chipset type that Garmin, Suunto, Polar, and COROS all use. Wahoo doesn’t allow you to change the recording rate, or GNSS type on RIVAL. Thus, it’s always set for 1-second recording with GPS+GLONASS. Therefore, that’s what I used in all my tests. Wahoo says that the watch is capable of Galileo, but they haven’t begun implementation or testing of that yet.</p> \n<p>First up, we’ll look at a run or two, then a ride, and then some swim data. For this first run, we’ll start with what should be a pretty dead simple GPS test.&nbsp; It’s literally a perfectly straight path with virtually no tree cover. It was an interval workout with my wife, and thus we made repeats back and forth along the path. It’s a good test to see how well the watch keeps the track on the path. In this case, it’s compared to the Polar GRIT X, and Garmin Forerunner 745 – both multisport watches. <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/ce943c8c-8c76-4ed7-7ff9-b62239069298\">Here’s that data set</a>:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-5.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-5.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"259\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>You can see the RIVAL in teal, and how the majority of the time on this stretch it was either significantly offset from the others, or slightly offset. While hard to see the blue on the GPS overlay below, you can see it’s off in the canal, and in particular, struggled going under the bridge:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-6.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-6.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"244\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>If we look at the 800m section of pathway that we did the majority of our intervals on, you can see the RIVAL was clearly offset much of the time in the canal. While I’m always up for a good canal swim, this one is bordered by free roaming horses, and they crap a lot. This would not be my preference for a canal swim location.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-7.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-7.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"240\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>That said, RIVAL did do better on this other straightaway next to the pony farms. I still wouldn’t swim there though.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-8.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-8.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"306\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I asked Wahoo about this particular set, as I thought it should have been a pretty easy use case. They said that at this point they haven’t really gotten to the full tuning of the GPS data, and thus they expect to see this improve more, likely cleaning up some of these nuances.</p> \n<p>And sometimes, other units get it wrong too. For <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/00e3f46a-5f54-4b69-7e42-78ba20d139d4\">example, a week or so later there’s this run</a> that started off on this same pathway. You can see that the RIVAL was still off in the canal (this time on the other side of the path, but at least the water is less horsey there). The FR745 was in the horse-crap-canal, and the Polar Grit X was actually on the path.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-9.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-9.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"243\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>But let’s head somewhere else, this time into the forest a bit for a longer loop. This time with the same crew of units, plus also the NURVV running shoe pods. Basically they’ve got GPS on the sides of the shoe clip-on pods.&nbsp; At a high level, <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/47656b80-1b0a-412b-4882-62ba8df09c20\">the watches in this data set all look pretty good</a>:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-10.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-10.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"379\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>But zooming in tells a different story. Setting aside the drunk NURVV GPS track, you can see the Wahoo RIVAL GPS track is often off smelling the (now very dead) flowers:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-11.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-11.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"271\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>It’s a pattern that would repeat itself throughout my testing. You can see how it’s constantly offset from the Garmin and Polar tracks, which are near identical.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-12.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-12.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"255\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Or the same elsewhere in the run:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-13.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-13.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"257\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Which again, doesn’t mean the others are perfect. You can see some slight wobbles from the Grit X and FR745 here in this section along the lake, but ultimately, the RIVAL had these wobbles far more frequently and far more impactfully than either the Garmin or Polar devices.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-14.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-14.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"251\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>So, let’s switch over to cycling and see how that rolls. And again, at a high level this looks pretty good. For <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/583d5010-7c1f-4642-7be7-c5cf640c7dae\">this set I did a route</a> through the forest and main roads, and then dove into a dedicated outdoor cycling track (width of a regular road) for endless loops. Portions of this are well forested.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-15.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-15.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"244\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>To begin, I go under this gigantic set of freeways and train tracks. It’s like the equivalent of a 10-12 lane road once everything is included, stretching over 100m wide with 3-4 different bridges. It’s really tricky for GPS units, and in this case, we can see that 3 out of 4 passes on this the RIVAL did fine, though it struggled a bit underneath. Note that on numerous other times I’ve passed under this bridge I didn’t see any notable issues.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-16.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-16.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"400\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>For this section passing through/past the woods, no issues here for the RIVAL:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-17.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-17.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"245\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Next, looking at the upper half of the cycle track (which is about 1.5mi/2.4km in length), we see that it’s largely very close. There’s a few times it’s peaking out here and there, but no more than the Karoo 2 is undercutting the corners slightly.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-18.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-18.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"334\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>From a cornering standpoint the FR745 is the most consistently on the road on each corner:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-19.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-19.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"301\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Same for the lower one. The Rival is the most consistently slightly offset. Largely not notable unless you really zoom in.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-20.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-20.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"247\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Though, it does occasionally canal dip:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-21.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-21.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"380\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Which, given its propensity to like going for a swim, maybe we should talk about GPS accuracy in openwater swims? Well, not well. <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/3fc85734-485d-4e65-4c87-be318c72adde\">Here’s an openwater swim session from yesterday</a>, with the FR745 on my other wrist also in openwater mode, and then a reference GPS atop a swim buoy floating behind me.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-22.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-22.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"368\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I’m not sure there’s really any value in zooming in on that one. The FR745 and swim buoy reference unit are almost identical. Scary impressive close actually.</p> \n<p>Just in case this might have been a one-off, here’s another openwater swim that I did last week, as <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/4eca20f0-58bd-4130-66b8-062a42ec0df9\">part of my mock-triathlon</a>:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-23.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-23.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"457\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>It too showed significant track errors.&nbsp; In talking to Wahoo about these specific swims, they believe there may be something antenna-wise on my unit. While they acknowledge the other land-based GPS tracks seemed to be about where they expect them, the openwater swim tracks are not at all what they expect.</p> \n<p>In fact, one of their engineers even shared a large data set of openwater swims with me – including GPS tracks from this very swim dock, showing quite reasonable openwater GPS accuracy to a swim buy reference GPS (another RIVAL in run mode). Nothing like what I’ve seen above.</p> \n<p>It sounds like they may be trying to get me another unit to go freeze my ass off again. Though, I suppose there’s probably not that many people in Europe or much of North America doing openwater swims this time of year (and the RIVAL isn’t yet shipping outside those two realms).</p> \n<p>Ultimately, in terms of GPS accuracy, the RIVAL as it stands today (ignoring the openwater issues), is kinda ‘meh’. It’s not as good as anything I’ve seen recently from Garmin, Polar, or COROS – but also isn’t bad either. If they can fix some of the more minor GPS meandering issues through software updates as they believe they can, then it’ll probably end up just like the others. If for no other reason than the fact that it’s likely all the exact same chipset anyway. But as always, software and antenna design play a huge role in overall device GPS accuracy.</p> \n<p><em>(Note: All of the charts in these accuracy sections were created using the DCR Analyzer tool.&nbsp; It allows you to compare power meters/trainers, heart rate, cadence, speed/pace, GPS tracks and plenty more. You can use it as well for your own gadget comparisons, </em><a href=\"http://www.dcrainmaker.com/analyzer\"><em>more details here</em></a><em>.)</em></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Heart Rate Accuracy:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1321.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1321\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1321_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1321\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Next up we’ve got heart rate accuracy.&nbsp; This roughly falls into two buckets: 24×7 HR, and workout HR.&nbsp; Unfortunately in the case of 24×7 data, there’s simply no way to validate that this time. Wahoo’s own app doesn’t display that data, and their connection at present to Apple’s HealthKit backend isn’t consistent enough to extract the data out. Thus, for now we’ll focus on the workout only data.</p> \n<p>Note that the Wahoo RIVAL uses an optical HR sensor from Philips. It’s been a pretty darn long time since we’ve heard of Philips in this realm. Last time that occurred <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2013/02/monitor-bluetooth-smartant.html\">was back in the Mio days</a>, where Mio licensed the Philips sensor for their initial products – and in fact, then sublicensed that to Garmin for Garmin’s FR225, the only Garmin wearable with a non-Garmin sensor. I’m not aware of any other mainstream wearable to use a Philips sensor since then, though, I do know they have actively been courting companies. I’m sure there are some watches out there with a Philips sensor but it’s just not disclosed.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1445.jpg\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1445\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1445_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1445\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Before we move on to the test results, note that optical HR sensor accuracy is rather varied from individual to individual.&nbsp; Aspects such as skin color, hair density, and position can impact accuracy.&nbsp; Position, and how the band is worn, are <strong>*the most important*</strong> pieces.&nbsp; A unit with an optical HR sensor should be snug.&nbsp; It doesn’t need to leave marks, but you shouldn’t be able to slide a finger under the band (at least during workouts).&nbsp; You can wear it a tiny bit looser the rest of the day.</p> \n<p>Ok, so in my testing, I simply use the watch throughout my normal workouts.&nbsp; Those workouts include a wide variety of intensities and conditions, making them great for accuracy testing.&nbsp; I’ve got steady runs, interval workouts on both bike and running.</p> \n<p>For each test, I’m wearing additional devices, usually 3-4 in total, which capture data from other sensors.&nbsp; Typically I’d wear a chest strap (usually the <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2020/09/garmin-hrm-pro-chest-strap-depth-review.html\">Garmin HRM-PRO</a> or <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2020/05/wahoos-new-2020-tickr-tickr-x-in-depth-review.html\">Wahoo TICKR X (2020 edition),</a> but also <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2020/01/polars-new-h9-heart-rate-strap-everything-you-ever-wanted-to-know.html\">Polar H9</a>) as well as another optical HR sensor watch on the other wrist (lately the Whoop band, <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2019/03/polar-oh1-plus-optical-hr-sensor-in-depth-review.html\">Polar OH1 Plus</a>). Note that the numbers you see in the upper right corner are *not* the averages, but rather just the exact point my mouse is sitting over.&nbsp; Note all this data is analyzed using the DCR Analyzer, <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/analyzer\">details here</a>.</p> \n<p>We’re going to start with <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/47656b80-1b0a-412b-4882-62ba8df09c20\">something simple here first</a>, a relatively stable run. This seems like it would be an easy test, though to add a tiny bit of difficulty, I did a 30-second hard interval every mile. The reddish-brown line below is the RIVAL. Aside from the Whoop strap, it’s obviously the one that sticks out the most.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-24.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-24.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"154\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>And ultimately, the above graph is basically RIVAL HR accuracy across a large pile of workouts, in a simple nutshell. It’s not great. It’s not horrific though either. It’s just a step below meh.</p> \n<p>If we zoom in on these sets, you can see that anytime I add intensity, the RIVAL optical HR sensor gets confused.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-25.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-25.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"167\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Let’s switch sports for a second. Here’s an <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/0beaa2fc-a604-4a66-6fe2-db38ea5d80e9\">indoor trainer ride on Zwift</a>. Pretty stable for all of it as you can see. And as you’d expect, the optical HR sensor is pretty much consistent with everyone else here.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-26.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-26.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"147\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>However, at the end I decide to throw-down two sprints. Well, one half-sprint (600w), and then one legit sprint (1,000w). You can see on the first one, RIVAL lost the plot but did manage to find it again half-way through (super rare for a sensor). However, on that second sprint, it totally lost it entirely. We can see that the TICKR-X was fastest, and then the FR745 – but then the FR745 lost the plot and the OH1 found the plot. The Whoop was late to the game, but then the RIVAL made a half-hearted belch and ultimately said ‘Nah, we’re good here.’</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-27.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-27.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"162\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>So you want an outside ride? Sure, <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/583d5010-7c1f-4642-7be7-c5cf640c7dae\">no problem</a>. Rival in blue this time.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-28.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-28.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"201\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Ok, that was less than ideal. Dance to your own beat or something.</p> \n<p>Now I do have this <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/5e74c34f-f699-4b41-5e68-df73cb05d705\">odd set here from a few weeks back</a>, but I think something was up there. Honestly, it’s just too perfect. Seriously, it’s virtually identical to the Polar H9 strap. So my guess is that despite not listing the paired sensors in the file (while the ELEMNT does this, the RIVAL doesn’t), I’m suspicious on this set that it might have paired behind the scenes.</p> \n<p>So, let’s look at another set. Here’s a shorter <a href=\"https://analyze.dcrainmaker.com/#/public/00e3f46a-5f54-4b69-7e42-78ba20d139d4\">run from last week</a>. This was pretty evenly paced, minus some intervals towards the end. You can see that the RIVAL, in blue, does reasonably well for the vast majority of it, save one big blip, and a few minor blips.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-29.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-29.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"150\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>And it tracks well in the intervals too. My guess is on that first interval below that the HRM-PRO chest strap did some cadence lock or something, as you can see it incorrectly spike high there.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-30.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-30.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"161\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>And here’s another run, this time intervals with my wife. I’d caution though that this isn’t high-intensity intervals for me though, as these cap-out at about my Z2 long-run heart rates. I point that out merely because intensity does matter here for accuracy. We see that for many of the intervals it does well, but it really struggles on the last couple 800’s, plus struggles on some of the sprints.</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-31.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-31.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"155\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Though equally, the FR745 struggled heavily on the 30” sprints here, as easily seen below:</p> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image-32.png\"><img style=\"border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"image\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/image_thumb-32.png\" alt=\"image\" width=\"722\" height=\"154\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>Note that the Polar Grit X was paired to the Polar H10 chest strap in this case.</p> \n<p>As for swimming heart rate? Well, it appears Wahoo has turned that off by default now for openwater swims. It was enabled last week on my openwater swim, but now it’s disabled. Maybe it’ll return. Note that you cannot do offloading of heart rate data from a TICKR strap (or any other strap). It sounds like that too is in the cards, but as noted, there’s a lot of cards on the table to sort and complete.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, I’d recommend using another heart rate sensor with the Wahoo RIVAL at this point, as the current optical HR sensor is just too prone to use either in daily non-interval usage, or in interval usage.</p> \n<h3><strong>Product Comparison:</strong></h3> \n<p>I’ve added the Wahoo RIVAL into the&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.dcrainmaker.com/product-comparison-calculator\">product comparison database</a>, allowing you to compare it against other products that I’ve reviewed in the past.&nbsp; For the purposes of below I’ve compared it against the Garmin FR745, Polar Grit X, Suunto 5, and COROS Pace 2. That’s perhaps a motley crew lineup, but it kinda works. One could argue doing COROS APEX instead of Pace 2 for a more polished look, or the Polar Vantage M instead of Grit X, or doing FR735XT instead of FR745 for better price but still more features.</p> make your own product comparison charts comparing any products using the&nbsp;<a href=\"http://www.dcrainmaker.com/product-comparison-calculator\">product comparison database</a>.</p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Summary:</span></h3> \n<p><a data-fancybox=\"gallery\" href=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1237.jpg\"><img style=\"margin: 0px; border: 0px currentcolor; display: inline; background-image: none;\" title=\"DSC_1237\" src=\"https://media.dcrainmaker.com/images/2020/11/DSC_1237_thumb.jpg\" alt=\"DSC_1237\" width=\"720\" height=\"480\" border=\"0\" /></a></p> \n<p>I’m excited about what Wahoo can do in this space. The journey to get to this point has been many years in the making, well before they truly started working on RIVAL (after all, the <a href=\"https://www.dcrainmaker.com/2013/07/magellan-echo.html\">Magellan Echo was actually a Wahoo watch</a>). Just as I’m excited to see COROS really finding their stride lately in products. Having competition is good for consumers – just as it was when Wahoo started in earnest with the ELEMNT series a few years back. But it was really the 2nd unit – the Wahoo BOLT, that pushed Garmin into responding. That was a great period of new features and increased benefits for the consumers.</p> \n<p>And there are a handful of awesome things about RIVAL. The touchless transitions is cool. Not so much for just going freestyle mid-race, but there in case you forget to press the button in the heat of the moment (or, double-press and need to undo mid-race). That’s great. Even more awesome is the app editor for super-precisely slicing and dicing your triathlon splits to the exact points on the map you want them to. Super cool stuff that nobody else is remotely doing.</p> \n<p>However, that doesn’t mean I’d recommend the RIVAL today, not in its current iteration. I think with enough money and developers, we’re probably about 8-12 months away from being able to compete with the likes of Suunto in certain areas (non-battery ones). Another year after that, maybe Polar (assuming Polar stopped developing entirely). Garmin? Well, that’s…who knows.</p> \n<p>And to be clear – this isn’t all about features. Though, one has to remember that while it’s easy to dismiss feature comparisons, the reality is that all of us value different features on different watches. One person’s ‘must-have’ feature is another persons ‘shrug’. That’s ultimately why products with more features do better – they appeal to a broader set of people. Products with less features can instead compete on accuracy, price, or simply brand love. Unfortunately, the RIVAL is easily the least accurate optical HR sensor watch I’ve tested in a while, and GPS isn’t great either. Price-wise, it’s almost double the price of the new (and fairly accurate) COROS Pace 2. Or one can pick up a Garmin Fenix 5 series watch for well under this price these days, which is both more accurate and more full featured. Or Polar…or Suunto…etc.</p> \n<p>And yes – I get it, Wahoo’s success in the bike computer market is all about simplicity over features. Polish over bugs. But RIVAL isn’t there today. It’s likely gonna be a while. And unlike a bike computer that you power off after the ride, a watch is on your wrist 24×7. It’s not the same world.</p> \n<p>Anyways, like I said – I’m looking forward to seeing where Wahoo goes here, and seeing where they are in 6 months, 12 months, etc… Plus, as they said – they’re
